<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">&nbsp;</font></b></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">HALC&#211;N RESOURCES CORPORATION</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">INFORMATION STATEMENT</font></b></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">PURSUANT TO SECTION&nbsp;14(f)&nbsp;OF</font></b></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">THE 
SECURITIES EXCHANGE ACT OF 1934</font></b></p>
<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">AND 
RULE 14F-1 THEREUNDER</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">THIS SCHEDULE IS BEING PROVIDED 
SOLELY FOR INFORMATIONAL PURPOSES AND NOT IN CONNECTION WITH ANY VOTE OF THE 
STOCKHOLDERS OF HALC&#211;N RESOURCES CORPORATION.</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">GENERAL</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">This Information Statement is being mailed or 
delivered to the stockholders of record of shares of common stock, par value 
$0.0001 per share (the &#147;<u>Common Stock</u>&#148;) of Halc&#243;n Resources
Corporation, a Delaware corporation (the &#147;<u>Company</u>&#148;) as of 
August&nbsp;30, 2016 with respect to a change of the majority of directors of 
the board of directors of the Company.&#160; This Information Statement is being
distributed on or about August&nbsp;31, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">On July&nbsp;27, 2016, the Company and certain of its 
subsidiaries filed voluntary petitions for relief (the &#147;<u>Bankruptcy 
Cases</u>&#148;) under chapter 11 of title 11 of the United States Code (the 
&#147;<u>Bankruptcy Code</u>&#148;) in the United States Bankruptcy Court for 
the District of Delaware in order to effect the Company&#146;s pre-packaged plan
of reorganization (the &#147;<u>Plan</u>&#148;). In connection with the Plan, 
the terms of the current members of the board of directors of the Company shall 
expire and the existing members shall approve the appointment of the members of 
a new board (the &#147;<u>New Board</u>&#148;), which shall take office on the 
effective date of the Plan (the &#147;<u>Effective Date</u>&#148;). The New 
Board shall be a nine (9)&nbsp;member board comprised of:</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;">i.</font><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>the chief executive officer of the 
Company;</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;">ii.</font><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160; </font>three (3)&nbsp;directors designated by Ares Management 
LLC (&#147;<u>Ares</u>&#148;) (provided that one such board selection shall be 
subject to the written consent of Franklin Advisers,&nbsp;Inc.
(&#147;<u>Franklin</u>&#148;), which consent shall not be unreasonably 
withheld);</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;">iii.</font><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; 
</font>three (3)&nbsp;directors designated by Franklin, (provided, in the cases 
of clauses (ii)&nbsp;and (iii)&nbsp;for so long as Ares or Franklin, 
respectively, continues to be a &#147;<u>Requisite Third Lien 
Noteholder</u>&#148; (as defined in the Plan to mean as of the date of 
determination, holders of the Company&#146;s 13.0% Senior Secured Notes due 2022
(the &#147;<u>Third Lien Notes</u>&#148;) that entered into that certain 
Restructuring Support Agreement dated as of June&nbsp;9, 2016 with the Company 
(&#147;<u>Consenting Third Lien Noteholders</u>&#148;), holding at least a 
majority in aggregate principal amount outstanding of the Third Lien Notes held 
by such Consenting Third Lien Noteholders as of such date; <u>provided</u> that 
Requisite Third Lien Noteholders shall include (a)&nbsp;Ares, for so long as it,
together with its affiliated funds that are Consenting Third Lien Noteholders, 
holds greater than 20% in aggregate principal outstanding amount of the Third 
Lien Notes, and (b)&nbsp;Franklin, for so long as it, together with its 
affiliated funds that are Consenting Third Lien Noteholders, holds greater than 
20% in aggregate principal outstanding amount of the Third Lien Notes) and, if 
Ares or Franklin is not a Requisite Third Lien Noteholder, then its three 
(3)&nbsp;directors shall be designated by Requisite Third Lien Noteholders (and 
if Franklin is not so included, it shall also lose its consent right to one of 
Ares&#146; board selections set forth above);</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-
align:center;">1<a name="PB_1_035617_7056"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade 
align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='1',FILE='C:\jms\109487\16-17636-1\task8083919\17636-1-
bc.htm',USER='109487',CD='Aug 30 04:11 2016' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;">iv.</font><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; 
</font>one (1)&nbsp;director designated by the holders of the Company&#146;s 
8.875% Senior Unsecured Notes, the 9.25% Senior Unsecured Notes, and the 9.75% 
Senior Unsecured Notes (the &#147;<u>Unsecured Notes</u>&#148;) that entered 
into that certain Restructuring Support Agreement dated as of June&nbsp;9, 2016 
with the Company (&#147;<u>Consenting Unsecured Noteholders</u>&#148;), holding 
at least a majority in aggregate principal amount outstanding of the Unsecured 
Notes held by the Consenting Unsecured Noteholders as of such date (the 
&#147;<u>Requisite Unsecured Noteholders</u>&#148;); <u>provided</u>, that any 
Unsecured Notes acquired by Ares and Franklin after June&nbsp;9, 2016 shall not 
be included in either the numerator or denominator of the foregoing calculation,
except for any Unsecured Notes acquired by them from other Consenting Unsecured 
Noteholders (the &#147;<u>Unsecured Director</u>&#148;); and</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;">v.</font><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160; </font>one (1)&nbsp;existing director of the Company designated by 
the chief executive officer of the Company, which shall be reasonably acceptable
to the Requisite Unsecured Noteholders and Requisite Third Lien Noteholders.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The New Board shall have a three-tiered structure 
classified into staggered 3-year terms, with two directors initially serving a 
one-year term, four directors (including the Unsecured Director) initially 
serving a two-year term, and three directors initially serving a three-year 
term.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Effective Date is expected to occur on or about 
September&nbsp;9, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The foregoing description of the Bankruptcy Cases and 
the Plan does not purport to be complete and is qualified in its entirety by the
terms of the Plan, which has been filed with the Securities and Exchange 
Commission (the &#147;<u>SEC</u>&#148;) as an exhibit to a Current Report on 
Form&nbsp;8-K filed June&nbsp;20, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">No action is required by our stockholders in 
connection with this Information Statement. The change of the majority of 
directors of the board will occur at or about the Effective Date. A stockholder 
vote is not required and will not be taken with respect to the appointment of 
the New Board. However, Section&nbsp;14(f)&nbsp;of the Exchange Act and 
Rule&nbsp;14f-1 promulgated thereunder require the mailing to our stockholders 
of record of the information set forth in this Information Statement. This 
Information Statement will be first mailed to the Company&#146;s stockholders of
record on or about August&nbsp;31, 2016.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Please read this Information Statement carefully. It 
contains certain biographical and other information concerning our executive 
officers and directors. All Company filings and exhibits thereto may be 
inspected without charge at the public reference section of the SEC at 100 F 
Street, N.E., Washington, DC 20549 or obtained on the SEC&#146;s website at 
www.sec.gov.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">VOTING SECURITIES</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">As of the date of this Information Statement, the 
Common Stock is the only class of equity securities that is currently 
outstanding and entitled to vote at a meeting of our stockholders. Each share of
Common Stock entitles the holder thereof to one vote. As of August&nbsp;29, 
2016, there are 122,629,925 shares of Common Stock issued and outstanding. No 
vote or other action of our stockholders is required in connection with this 
Information Statement.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">This Information Statement is being provided solely 
for informational purposes not in connection with any vote of the stockholders
of the Company. No proxies are being solicited and you are not requested to send
a proxy.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pursuant to the terms of the Plan, on the Effective 
Date holders of Third Lien Notes will receive their pro rata share of 76.5% of 
the Common Stock, holders of Unsecured Notes will receive their pro rata share 
of 15.5% of the Common Stock, the holder of the 8.0% Senior Unsecured 
Convertible Note due 2020 issued on February&nbsp;8, 2012 will receive 4% of the
Common Stock and existing common stock holders will receive</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-
align:center;">2<a name="PB_2_035634_5335"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade 
align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">their pro rata share of 4% of the Common Stock.&#160; 
Each of the foregoing percentage allocations regarding Common Stock are subject 
to dilution by a management incentive plan and the exercise of new warrants 
granted to holders of Unsecured Notes and the holder of the 8.0% Senior 
Unsecured Convertible Note, each as described in more detail in the Plan.&#160; 
The issuance of the Common Stock as described above is exempt from registration 
pursuant to section 1145(a)&nbsp;of the Bankruptcy Code.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">A change of the majority of directors of the board is 
expected to occur as a result of the transactions contemplated by the Plan, as 
described above. Following the Effective Date, the Company expects the Board 
will be comprised of William J. Campbell, James W. Christmas, Michael L. Clark, 
Thomas R. Fuller, Darryl Schall, Ronald D. Scott, Eric G. Takaha, Nathan W. 
Walton and Floyd C. Wilson, the appointment of each of whom will be approved by 
the current board.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Floyd
C. Wilson</font></b> became Chairman and Chief Executive Officer in 
February&nbsp;2012. Prior to February&nbsp;2012, he was President of HALRES LLC,
an oil and natural gas company that he founded in October&nbsp;2011. 
Mr.&nbsp;Wilson served as Chairman of the Board and Chief Executive Officer of 
Petrohawk Energy Corporation from May&nbsp;25, 2004 until BHP Billiton acquired 
Petrohawk for $15.1 billion, including assumed debt, in August&nbsp;2011. 
Mr.&nbsp;Wilson also served as President of Petrohawk from May&nbsp;25, 2004 
until September&nbsp;8, 2009. Prior to May&nbsp;25, 2004, he was President and 
Chief Executive Officer of PHAWK, LLC which he founded in June&nbsp;2003. 
Mr.&nbsp;Wilson was the Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of 3TEC Energy 
Corporation from August&nbsp;1999 until its merger with Plains 
Exploration&nbsp;&amp; Production Company in June&nbsp;2003. Mr.&nbsp;Wilson 
founded W/E Energy Company L.L.C., formerly known as 3TEC Energy Company L.L.C. 
in 1998 and served as its President until August&nbsp;1999. Mr.&nbsp;Wilson 
began his career in the energy business in Houston, Texas in 1970 as a 
completion engineer. He moved to Wichita, Kansas in 1976 to start an oil and gas
operating company, one of several private energy ventures which preceded the 
formation of Hugoton Energy Corporation in 1987, where he served as Chairman, 
President and Chief Executive Officer. In 1994, Hugoton completed an initial 
public offering and was merged into Chesapeake Energy Corporation in 1998.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font

weight:bold;">Tucker S. Bridwell</font></b> became a director in 
February&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Bridwell served as a director of Petrohawk Energy 
Corporation from May&nbsp;2004 until December&nbsp;2010. Mr.&nbsp;Bridwell has 
been the President of Mansefeldt Investment Corporation and the Dian Graves Owen
Foundation since September&nbsp;1997 and</p>

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"
style="font-size:10.0pt;">manages investments in both entities. He has been in 
the energy business in various capacities for over 27 years, focusing on oil and
gas private equity and public oil and gas investments with extensive experience 
in managing both public and private energy companies. Mr.&nbsp;Bridwell is a 
Certified Public Accountant and has practiced public accountancy, specializing 
in oil and gas. He earned a Bachelor of Business Administration degree and a 
Master of Business Administration degree from Southern Methodist University. He 
has also served on the audit committees of numerous businesses, including 
Petrohawk and non-profit organizations. Currently, he serves on the board of 
directors of Concho Resources,&nbsp;Inc. and First Financial 
Bankshares,&nbsp;Inc. He is also Lead Director and Chairman of the Nominating 
and Corporate Governance Committee of First Financial Bankshares,&nbsp;Inc. 
Mr.&nbsp;Bridwell previously served as Chairman of First Permian, LLC from 2000 
until its sale to Energen Corporation in April&nbsp;2002.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">John 
W. Brown</font></b> became a director in March&nbsp;2016. Since June&nbsp;2005, 
Mr.&nbsp;Brown has served as Chairman of Par Investments, LLC, a private 
investment firm focused on energy related investments, and since July&nbsp;1991,
he has served as the General Partner of Premier Capital,&nbsp;Ltd., a private 
energy focused investment banking firm. From 2001 to 2003, Mr.&nbsp;Brown served
as a Director of Friedman, Billings, Ramsey Group, a publicly traded full 
service banking firm focused on energy investment banking transactions. Prior to
that, Mr.&nbsp;Brown served as an Associate of Private Energy Capital Investment
at EnCap Investments, L.C. from 2000 to 2001; as the Founder and General Partner
of WesAl Capital,&nbsp;Ltd., a private energy investment banking firm with the 
late William E. Simon, former Secretary of the Treasury and Alvin Shoemaker, 
former Chairman of First Boston from 1986 to 1991; and as the Founder, 
Shareholder and President of Westwood Resources Company, a privately held 
independent oil and gas company, from 1981 to 1984. Mr.&nbsp;Brown practiced law
from 1973 until 1981. He earned a Bachelor of Arts Degree from Southern 
Methodist University and a Juris Doctor Degree and Master of Laws Degree from 
Southern Methodist University Law School.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">James
W. Christmas</font></b> became a director in February&nbsp;2012. 
Mr.&nbsp;Christmas began serving as a director of Petrohawk Energy Corporation 
on July&nbsp;12, 2006, effective upon the merger of KCS Energy,&nbsp;Inc. 
(&#147;KCS&#148;) into Petrohawk. He continued to serve as a director, and as 
Vice Chairman of the Board of Directors, for Petrohawk until BHP Billiton 
acquired all of Petrohawk in August&nbsp;2011. He also served on the Audit 
Committee and the Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee. 
Mr.&nbsp;Christmas served as a member of the Board of Directors of Petrohawk, a 
wholly-owned subsidiary of BHP Billiton, and as chair of the Financial Reporting
Committee of such board until September&nbsp;2014. He also serves on the 
Advisory Board of the Tobin School of Business of St. John&#146;s University. 
Mr.&nbsp;Christmas serves as a director of Rice Energy, as chairman of its audit
committee and a member of its compensation committee, and as a director and 
member of the audit committee and compensation committee of Yuma Energy. He 
served as President and Chief Executive Officer of KCS from 1988 until 
April&nbsp;2003 and Chairman of the Board and Chief Executive Officer of KCS 
until its merger into Petrohawk. Mr.&nbsp;Christmas was a Certified Public 
Accountant in New York and was with Arthur Andersen&nbsp;&amp; Co. from 1970 
until 1978 before leaving to join National Utilities&nbsp;&amp; Industries 
(&#147;NUI&#148;), a diversified energy company, as Vice President and 
Controller. He remained with NUI until 1988, when NUI spun out its unregulated 
activities that ultimately became part of KCS. As an auditor and audit manager, 
controller and in his role as CEO of KCS, Mr.&nbsp;Christmas was directly or 
indirectly responsible for financial reporting and compliance with SEC 
regulations, and as such has extensive experience in reviewing and evaluating
financial reports, as well as in evaluating executive and board performance and 
in recruiting directors.</p>

acquisition, drilling and production company which also invests in other energy-
related companies. Mr.&nbsp;Fuller has earned degrees</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">from the University of Wyoming and the Louisiana State
University School of Banking of the South and is a Registered Professional 
Engineer in Texas. He has 48 years of experience as a petroleum engineer, 
specializing in economic and reserves evaluation. He has served as an employee, 
officer, partner or director of various companies, including ExxonMobil, First 
City National Bank, Hillin Oil Co., Diverse Energy Management Co. and Rimco 
Royalty Partners. In February&nbsp;2015, Mr.&nbsp;Fuller became a director of 
Azure Midstream Partners LP, a public company traded on the NYSE, and serves as 
a member of its Audit Committee. Mr.&nbsp;Fuller also serves as a director of 
privately held Azure Midstream Holdings. Mr.&nbsp;Fuller also has extensive 
experience in energy-related merger and acquisition transactions, having 
generated and closed over 90 producing property acquisitions during his career. 
As a primary lending officer to many independent energy companies, 
Mr.&nbsp;Fuller has extensive experience in analyzing and evaluating financial, 
business and operational strategies for energy companies.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font

E. Godwin</font></b> became a director in December&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Godwin 
currently serves as a Senior Principal of Canada Pension Plan Investment Board 
in its Relationship Investments group, a position he has held since 2008. From 
2005 to 2008, Mr.&nbsp;Godwin served as a Principal of Birch Hill Equity 
Partners L.P. From 1995 to 2005, he worked at TD Securities then TD Capital 
Group Limited, ultimately serving as Vice President and Director. 
Mr.&nbsp;Godwin began his professional career in 1989 with ICI Explosives then 
Stuart Energy serving as a Project Engineer. Mr.&nbsp;Godwin is a graduate of 
Queen&#146;s University (Kingston, Ontario), having received a Bachelor&#146;s 
Degree in Applied Science (Mechanical Engineering) in 1989. He also received a 
Masters Degree in Business Administration in 1995 from the Richard Ivey School 
of Business, University of Western Ontario. In 2012, Mr.&nbsp;Godwin received 
the ICD.D designation from the Institute of Corporate Directors. Mr.&nbsp;Godwin
has served on the board of directors of several private companies.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Paul 
P. Huffard IV</font></b> became a director in March&nbsp;2016. Mr.&nbsp;Huffard 
currently serves as a Senior Advisor on the Advisory Counsel of Strategic Value 
Partners, a distressed and deep-value private equity firm. He also serves as 
Chairman of the Board of Directors of Vubiq Networks,&nbsp;Inc., a privately 
held wireless networking technology firm, and on the Board of Directors of CORE 
Media Group. From 1995 to 2014, Mr.&nbsp;Huffard served as a Senior Managing 
Director of The Blackstone Group where he provided financial and strategic 
advice to companies and creditors in situations involving financial 
restructuring, as well as to corporate parents and purchasers of distressed 
companies. Mr.&nbsp;Huffard&#146;s areas of expertise include business plan 
development, capital structure analysis and structuring, capital raising, 
mergers and acquisitions, valuation, negotiation and expert witness testimony. 
Prior to joining The Blackstone Group in 1995, Mr.&nbsp;Huffard gained 
investment banking experience at Smith, Barney, Harris, Upham&nbsp;&amp; Co. and
Hellmold Associates. He earned a Bachelor of Administration degree in Economics 
from Harvard College and a Master of Business Administration degree from the 
Kellogg School of Management at Northwestern University.</p>

Republic National Bank of Dallas, ultimately serving as Vice President and 
Manager of the bank&#146;s wholly-owned subsidiary, Republic Energy Finance 
Corporation. Mr.&nbsp;Miller is a graduate of Southern Methodist University, 
having received Bachelors and Masters Degrees in Business Administration in 1972
and 1973, respectively. He serves on the Board of Trustees at Southern Methodist
University and also is a member of the Executive Board of the Edwin L. Cox 
School of Business. Mr.&nbsp;Miller is a recipient of Distinguished Alumnus 
Awards from both Southern Methodist University and the Cox School. In 2004, 
Mr.&nbsp;Miller was appointed to the National Petroleum Council, an advisory 
body to the Secretary of Energy, and he is a member of the Board of Advisors of 
the Maguire Energy Institute. Additionally, he is a member of the Independent 
Petroleum Association of America, the Texas Independent</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Daniel A. Rioux</font></b> became a director in 
February&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Rioux is a Founder and Managing Partner of Old 
Ironsides Energy, LLC, an oil and gas investment firm that manages a multi-
billion dollar portfolio. From April&nbsp;2009 to August&nbsp;2013, 
Mr.&nbsp;Rioux was Co-President and Chief Executive Officer of Liberty Energy 
Holdings, LLC. From 2001 to 2008, Mr.&nbsp;Rioux served as Vice President of 
Liberty Energy Holdings, LLC, where he had responsibility for all of the 
company&#146;s investment and management decisions. From 1993 until 2000, 
Mr.&nbsp;Rioux was employed by Liberty Energy Corporation, a subsidiary of 
Liberty Energy Holdings, LLC. Mr.&nbsp;Rioux currently serves as a director of 
Vermilion Cliffs Partners, a Fort Worth, Texas-based exploration and production 
company and Axia Energy, LLC, a Denver-based exploration and production company,
as well as a manager of Discovery Midstream Holdings LLC, a Dallas-based company
focused on the development, acquisition and operation of gas gathering and 
midstream oil and gas assets and Wildcat Midstream Holdings LLC, a company 
focused on the development, acquisition and operation of gas gathering and 
midstream oil and gas assets. Mr.&nbsp;Rioux previously served as a Director of 
Petrohawk Energy Corporation from 2004 to 2006 and as a director of Energy 
Transfer Equity from 2002 to 2006. He also served as a director of the 
Independent Petroleum Association of America from 2003 to 2011. Mr.&nbsp;Rioux 
holds a B.S. in Finance from Bryant College and an M.B.A from Babson 
College.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Michael A. Vlasic</font></b> became a director in 
August&nbsp;2012. Prior to his appointment as a director of the Company, 
Mr.&nbsp;Vlasic served on the board of directors of GeoResources,&nbsp;Inc. 
since April&nbsp;2007. He also served on the board of managers of Southern Bay 
Energy, LLC from its inception in 2004 until it was acquired by GeoResources in 
April&nbsp;2007. He previously was a Director of Texoil,&nbsp;Inc., where he 
served on its executive committee from 1997 until its sale to Ocean Energy Inc. 
in 2001. From July&nbsp;1989 to December&nbsp;2013 he served as Chief Executive 
Manager of Vlasic Investments L.L.C. In January&nbsp;2014 he founded a private 
investment company, NBT Investments LLC. He is the founder and a Director of MAV
Development Company. Mr.&nbsp;Vlasic has served in various executive positions, 
including CFO and President, of private companies in a variety of industries; 
including automobile and truck fleeting leasing, computer equipment leasing and 
services, oil and gas exploration and production, aircraft maintenance, 
management and leasing, and real estate development and construction. He has 
served on the investment committee of venture capital, private equity and direct
lending investment funds. Mr.&nbsp;Vlasic serves on the board of Bessemer Trust 
Company and some of its affiliates. He also serves on the investment committee 
of HV Capital Investors. He is a 1982 graduate of Brown University and holds an 
MBA from the University of Michigan.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Mark 
A. Welsh IV</font></b> became a director in February&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Welsh 
currently serves as a Managing Director of EnCap Investments L.P. Mr.&nbsp;Welsh
has 15 years of experience in private equity, including 10 years with EnCap. 
Prior to joining EnCap, Mr.&nbsp;Welsh served as a financial analyst with The 
Blackstone Group L.P. and as a Vice President with Adam Corporation. 
Mr.&nbsp;Welsh serves on the board of directors of several EnCap portfolio 
companies. Mr.&nbsp;Welsh received a Bachelor of Business Administration degree 
in Finance from Texas A&amp;M University, where he was recognized with the 
Brown-Rudder Award as the outstanding graduate in his class.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Stephen W. Herod</font></b>&nbsp;has served as President since 
May&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Herod served as Executive Vice President&#151;Corporate 
Development and Assistant Secretary of Petrohawk Energy Corporation from 
August&nbsp;2005 until BHP Billiton acquired Petrohawk in August&nbsp;2011. 
Mr.&nbsp;Herod served as Vice President&#151;Corporate Development of Petrohawk 
from May&nbsp;2004 until August&nbsp;2005. Prior to joining Petrohawk, he was 
employed by PHAWK,&nbsp;LLC from its formation in June&nbsp;2003 until 
May&nbsp;2004. He served as Executive Vice President&#151;Corporate Development 
for 3TEC Energy Corporation from December&nbsp;1999 until its merger with Plains
Exploration&nbsp;&amp; Production Company in June&nbsp;2003 and as Assistant 
Secretary from May&nbsp;2001 until June&nbsp;2003. Mr.&nbsp;Herod served as a 
director of 3TEC from July&nbsp;1997 until January&nbsp;2002. Mr.&nbsp;Herod 
served as the Treasurer of 3TEC from 1999 until 2001. From July&nbsp;1997 to
December&nbsp;1999, Mr.&nbsp;Herod was Vice President&#151;Corporate Development
of 3TEC. Mr.&nbsp;Herod served as President and a director of Shore Oil Company 
from April&nbsp;1992 until the merger of Shore with 3TEC&#146;s predecessor in 
June&nbsp;1997. He joined Shore&#146;s predecessor as Controller in 
February&nbsp;1991. Mr.&nbsp;Herod was employed by Conquest Exploration Company 
from 1984 until 1991 in various financial management positions, including 
Operations Accounting Manager. From 1981 to 1984, Superior Oil Company employed 
Mr.&nbsp;Herod as a financial analyst. Mr.&nbsp;Herod has a Bachelor of Science 
degree in finance and management from Oklahoma State University.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font

J. Mize</font></b>&nbsp;has served as Executive Vice President, Chief Financial 
Officer and Treasurer since February&nbsp;2012. Mr.&nbsp;Mize served as 
Executive Vice President&#151;Chief Financial Officer and Treasurer of Petrohawk
Energy Corporation from August&nbsp;2007 until BHP Billiton acquired Petrohawk 
in August&nbsp;2011. Mr.&nbsp;Mize served as the Chief Ethics Officer and 
Insider Trading Compliance Officer for Petrohawk until June&nbsp;2009. 
Additionally, he served as Vice President, Chief Accounting Officer and 
Controller at Petrohawk from July&nbsp;2005 until August&nbsp;2007. 
Mr.&nbsp;Mize first joined Petrohawk in November&nbsp;2004 as Controller. Prior 
to working at Petrohawk, Mr.&nbsp;Mize was the Manager of Financial Reporting of
Cabot Oil&nbsp;&amp; Gas Corporation, a public oil and gas exploration company, 
from January&nbsp;2003 to November&nbsp;2004. Prior to his employment at Cabot 
Oil&nbsp;&amp; Gas Corporation, he was an Audit Manager with 
PricewaterhouseCoopers&nbsp;LLP from 1996 to 2002. Mr.&nbsp;Mize is a Certified 
Public Accountant and has a Bachelor degree in Accounting from the University of
Houston.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The following paragraphs contain certain information 
about each of the members of the New Board, other than that of 
Messrs.&nbsp;Wilson, Christmas and Fuller, current directors whose biographical 
information is included above.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">William J. Campbell</font></b>.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Campbell is the 
Managing Director and Co-owner of CB Energy, LLC, an independent oil and gas 
exploration company founded in 1997.&#160; He has over thirty two years of 
experience in the legal, investment and energy industries with a diverse 
background in management, finance, legal, land and marketing.&#160; Since 2006, 
Mr.&nbsp;Campbell has served as owner and managing director of PPPCo-CB Energy, 
LLC, a Houston, Texas-based private oil and gas exploration and production 
company.&#160; From 1991 to 1996, Mr.&nbsp;Campbell served as Principal, Vice 
President and Corporate Counsel of Houston, Texas-based Fremont Energy 
Corporation, a Bechtel Family company, where Mr.&nbsp;Campbell managed the 
company&#146;s domestic and international energy asset portfolio and directed 
the company&#146;s commercial, banking, and legal activities, and from 1985 
through 1991, Mr.&nbsp;Campbell served as Counsel and Manager for Bechtel 
Investments,&nbsp;Inc. in Houston, Texas, managing its oil and gas marketing and
land/legal operations.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Campbell was also the first representative
of Bechtel in the J.P. Morgan Corporate Finance Program, New York, New York 
(1988).&#160; In addition, Mr.&nbsp;Campbell represented Bechtel&#146;s outside 
oil and gas interests by serving as a Director on the boards of BecField 
Drilling Services, the then largest independent horizontal and directional 
drilling company in the United States, CurveDrill,&nbsp;Inc. and PetroSource 
Corporation, a refining and marketing company with annual revenues over $500 
million.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Campbell started his professional career at the Houston,
Texas law firm of Reynolds, Allen&nbsp;&amp; Cook.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Campbell has a
Doctorate of Jurisprudence (J.D.) and holds a Bachelor of Business 
Administration Degree (BBA) in Petroleum Land Management/Finance from the</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">University of Texas in Austin, Texas.&#160; 
Mr.&nbsp;Campbell is active in community and civic affairs.&#160; His service 
includes:&#160; The Kinkaid School Board of Trustees of Houston since 2007, and 
its Advancement, Finance&nbsp;&amp; Building Committees since 2002; the Board of
Directors of the Houston Country Club from 2005 to 2007; the Institute for 
Molecular Medicine as a Founding Trustee and Scientific Advisory Board Member 
since 2001; the Development Board of the University of Texas Health Science 
Center since 1991- <i>Chair Emeritus</i> 2002-2003; the Advisory Boards of 
Tanglewood Bank, NA and the Amegy Bank of Texas, N.A. since 1998; the Endowment 
Board,&nbsp;Jr. Warden and Senior Council Representative of St. Martin&#146;s 
Episcopal Church since 2004;&#160; the Board of Directors and Treasurer of the
Daniel and Edith Ripley Foundation since 2005; the Board of Directors of the 
Bayou City Pump Inc. since 2010; the Board of Directors of Erin Energy 
Corporation and its Audit and Compensation Committees since 2011; the Advance 
Team Board of M.D. Anderson since 2005; the Texas Children&#146;s Hospital 
Individuals Committee since 2005; the Memorial Hermann System Board of Directors
and its Finance and Chairman-Governance Committees and Memorial Hermann 
Foundation since 2011 and a Member of the Texas Bar Association.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Michael L. Clark</font></b>.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Clark is a Chartered 
Financial Analyst (CFA) Charterholder with seventeen years of investing 
experience focusing on basic materials and oilfield services and equipment 
equities.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Clark served as a Retired Partner of SIR Capital 
Management, LLC from 2014 until his retirement in 2016 and from 2008 to 2013, as
a Portfolio Manager and Partner.&#160; Prior to that, Mr.&nbsp;Clark valued 
energy equities as a portfolio manager at Satellite Asset Management, LLC from 
2005 to 2007 and as an equity research analyst at SAC Capital Management, LLC 
from 2003 to 2005 and at Merrill Lynch from 1997 to 2002.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Clark 
began his career at Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche, LLP, becoming a CPA and Senior 
Auditor within its Securities Industry Auditing Group.&#160; He graduated cum 
laude from the University of Pennsylvania with a Bachelor of Arts in Economics 
and earned a Masters of Business Administration in Finance and Economics from 
New York University&#146;s Stern School of Business.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Darryl Schall</font></b>.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Schall is a Partner and 
Portfolio Manager in the Ares Private Equity Group, where he is responsible for 
managing Ares&#146; special situations strategy.&#160; Additionally, he serves 
on the Investment Committee for the Ares Special Situations funds.&#160; Prior 
to joining Ares in 2009, Mr.&nbsp;Schall worked at Tudor Investment Corporation,
where he focused on managing distressed and high yield investments.&#160; 
Previously, Mr.&nbsp;Schall was a Managing Director and Director of High Yield 
Research at Trust Company of the West, where he focused on managing portfolios 
of distressed and high yield debt.&#160; In addition, Mr.&nbsp;Schall was a 
Senior Research Analyst and Senior Vice President at Dabney/Resnick&nbsp;&amp; 
Wagner,&nbsp;Inc., a boutique investment firm specializing in high yield and 
distressed debt.&#160; Previously, Mr.&nbsp;Schall was an Investment Banking 
Associate of the Corporate Finance Department of Drexel Burnham Lambert Inc. and
was a Supervising Senior Accountant with KPMG Peat Marwick.&#160; 
Mr.&nbsp;Schall holds a B.A., cum laude, from the University of California, Los 
Angeles, in History and an M.B. A. from the University of Chicago.&#160; 
Mr.&nbsp;Schall also is a Certified Public Accountant.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Ronald D. Scott</font></b>.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Scott has over thirty 
years oil and gas industry experience.&#160; Most recently, from 2013 to 2016, 
Mr.&nbsp;Scott served as President and CEO of True Oil Company, a private equity
backed oil and gas firm.&#160; Prior to that, from 1996 to 2012, he served as 
President and Chief Operating Officer of Midland, Texas-based Henry Petroleum 
and its successor companies, Henry Resources and HPC Energy.&#160; During this 
time, Mr.&nbsp;Scott successfully led the sale and re-start of multiple 
companies.&#160; Beginning his career with Exxon Corporation, from 1983 to 1995,
Mr.&nbsp;Scott held various supervisory and managerial assignments in 
Engineering, Operations, Planning and Financial Accounting and Reporting.&#160; 
In addition to the Permian Basin, he had assignments covering operational areas 
in the Gulf Coast/Gulf of Mexico region, California and the Rocky 
Mountains.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Scott was the Technical Manager for Exxon&#146;s 
multi-billion dollar onshore operations in the Western United States and prior
to joining Henry Petroleum.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Scott serves as a Director of 
Blackbrush Oil and Gas and Pardus Oil and Gas and as the Vice President of the 
Board of the Henry Foundation, a founding member of Educate Midland and on the 
Chamber of</p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Commerce.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Scott holds Master and 
Bachelor of Science degrees in Engineering from New Mexico State University and 
is a Registered Petroleum Engineer in the State of Texas.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Eric 
G. Takaha</font></b>.&#160; Prior to his retirement in 2016, Mr.&nbsp;Takaha 
served as a Portfolio Manager, Senior Vice President and Director of the 
Corporate and High Yield Group at Franklin Templeton Investments.&#160; He also 
served as a member of the firm&#146;s Fixed Income Policy Committee, which 
helped guide investment strategies for multi-sector fixed income accounts.&#160;
At Franklin Templeton Investments, Mr.&nbsp;Takaha managed multiple fixed income
portfolios, with a focus on those with corporate credit investments, as well as 
overseeing and directing the firm&#146;s group of high yield and investment 
grade credit analysts as they formulated investment recommendations.&#160; He 
originally joined Franklin Templeton Investments in 1989, and served as a 
research analyst covering a number of different industries.&#160; 
Mr.&nbsp;Takaha currently serves as Treasurer and on the Board of the Redwood 
City Educational Foundation, on the Finance Committee for Make A Wish (San 
Francisco), on the Investment Sub-Committee for Catholic Charities (San 
Francisco) and as a mentor in the Friends for Youth organization.&#160; He 
received his B.S. from the University of California Berkeley in 1989 and his 
M.B.A from Stanford University in 1996.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Takaha is a Chartered 
Financial Analyst (CFA) Charterholder since 1993 and serves as a member of the 
CFA Society of San Francisco, the CFA Institute and the Standard Business School
Alumni Association.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><b><font 
size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
weight:bold;">Nathan W. Walton</font></b>.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Walton is a Partner in
the Ares Private Equity Group and joined the firm in 2006.&#160; Additionally, 
he serves on the Investment Committee for Ares EIF funds.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Walton 
has experience managing investments in, and serving on the Boards of Directors 
of, companies operating in various industries, including in the oil and natural 
gas exploration and production industry.&#160; Currently, Mr.&nbsp;Walton serves
on the Boards of Directors of Clayton Williams Energy,&nbsp;Inc. and the parent 
company of BlackBrush Oil&nbsp;&amp; Gas, L.P.&#160; Mr.&nbsp;Walton holds a 
B.A. from Princeton University in Politics and an M.B.A. from the Stanford 
Graduate School of Business.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">DIRECTOR INDEPENDENCE</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The board has determined that each of 
Messrs.&nbsp;Bridwell, Brown, Christmas, Fuller, Godwin, Huffard, Miller, Rioux,
Vlasic and Welsh is an &#147;independent director&#148; as evaluated under the 
standards for director independence established by our guidelines and applicable
laws, rules&nbsp;and listing standards, including, without limitation, the 
standards for independent directors established by the New York Stock 
Exchange,&nbsp;Inc. and the SEC.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">CORPORATE GOVERNANCE</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Information Concerning Operation of 
the Board</font></i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our board of directors has the responsibility for 
establishing our broad corporate policies and for our overall performance. 
However, the board of directors is not involved in our day-to-day operations. 
The board of directors is kept informed of our business through discussions with
our Chairman and Chief Executive Officer and other officers, by reviewing 
analyses and reports provided to it on a regular basis, and by participating in 
board of directors and committee meetings. Our board of directors held 13 
meetings during 2015, including telephonic meetings, and acted by unanimous 
written consent 10 times, and all directors attended at least 75% of the total 
meetings of the board of directors and the committees on which such director 
served during the fiscal year.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our board of directors currently has four standing 
committees: Audit, Compensation, Nominating and Corporate Governance, and 
Reserves. Actions taken by our committees are reported to the full board 
of</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-
align:center;">11<a name="PB_11_035541_5335"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade 
align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">directors. Each committee conducts an annual 
evaluation of its duties and is expected to conduct an annual review of its 
respective charter.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" 
face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Audit 
Committee.</font></i>&#160; The members of our Audit Committee are James W. 
Christmas, Kevin E. Godwin and Mark A. Welsh IV, with Mr.&nbsp;Christmas serving
as the chairman. Our board of directors has determined that all members of our 
audit committee are financially literate within the meaning of SEC rules, under 
the current listing standards of the NYSE and in accordance with our audit 
committee charter. Our board of directors has also determined that all members 
of the audit committee are independent, within the meaning of SEC and NYSE 
regulations for independence for audit committee members, under our corporate 
governance guidelines, and in accordance with our audit committee charter. The 
board of directors has also determined that Mr.&nbsp;Christmas is an &#147;audit
committee financial expert&#148; (as defined under SEC rules).</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Audit Committee is responsible for oversight of 
Company risks relating to accounting matters, financial reporting and related 
legal and regulatory compliance. The Audit Committee annually considers the 
qualifications and evaluates the performance of our independent auditor and 
selects and engages our independent auditor. The Audit Committee meets quarterly
with representatives of the independent auditor and is available to meet at the 
request of the independent auditor. During these meetings, the Audit Committee 
receives reports regarding our books of accounts, accounting procedures, 
financial statements, audit policies and procedures, internal accounting and 
financial controls, and other matters within the scope of the Audit 
Committee&#146;s duties. The Audit Committee reviews the plans for and the 
results of audits for us and our subsidiaries. The Audit Committee reviews the 
independence of the independent auditor, and considers and authorizes the fees 
for both audit and non-audit services provided by the independent auditor. In 
2015, our Audit Committee held four meetings.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" 
face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Compensation 
Committee.&#160; </font></i>The members of our Compensation Committee are Tucker
S. Bridwell, Daniel A. Rioux, Michael A. Vlasic and Mark A. Welsh IV, with 
Mr.&nbsp;Vlasic serving as the chairman. Our board of directors has determined 
that each member of the Compensation Committee meets the NYSE standards for 
independence, and is a &#147;non-employee director&#148; as defined in 
Rule&nbsp;16b-3 under the Exchange Act, an &#147;outside director&#148; as 
defined for purposes of Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;of the Internal Revenue Code of
1986, as amended, and the enhanced independence requirements set forth in 
Rule&nbsp;10C-1 under the Exchange Act.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Compensation Committee is entrusted with the 
overall responsibility for establishing, implementing and monitoring the 
compensation for our executive officers (our chief executive officer, president,
each executive vice president, and each senior vice president). The Compensation
Committee also administers our First Amended and Restated 2012 Long-Term 
Incentive Plan, or Plan, and approves restricted stock, stock option, and 
performance awards and other stock-based grants for our executive officers. In 
2015, our Compensation Committee held seven meetings, including telephonic 
meetings and acted by unanimous written consent one time.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" 
face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Nominating 
and Corporate Governance Committee.</font></i> &#160;The members of our 
Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee are Thomas R. Fuller, Daniel A. 
Rioux and Michael A. Vlasic, with Mr.&nbsp;Rioux serving as the chairman. Our 
board of directors has determined that all members of the Nominating and 
Corporate Governance Committee are independent pursuant to the NYSE rules, under
our corporate governance guidelines, and in accordance with our nominating and 
corporate governance committee charter.</p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee is 
responsible for identifying qualified candidates to be presented to our board of
directors for nomination as directors, ensuring that our board of directors and 
our organizational documents are structured in a way that best serves our 
practices and objectives, and developing and recommending a set of corporate 
governance principles. The Nominating and Corporate Governance Committee may 
consider candidates for our board of directors from any reasonable source, 
including a search firm engaged by the Nominating and Corporate Governance 
Committee,</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LEGAL PROCEEDINGS INVOLVING DIRECTORS
AND EXECUTIVE OFFICERS</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">To our knowledge, except as otherwise described 
herein, there have been no events under any bankruptcy act, no criminal 
proceedings and no Federal or State judicial or administrative orders, judgments
or decrees or findings, no violations of any Federal or State securities law, 
and no violations of any Federal commodities law material to the evaluation of 
the ability and integrity of any director (existing or proposed) or executive 
officer of the Company during the past ten (10)&nbsp;years. The Company is not 
aware of any legal proceedings in which any director, officer, or any owner of 
record or beneficial owner of more than 5% of any class of voting securities of 
the Company, or any affiliate of any such director, officer, affiliate of the 
Company, or security holder, or any person who will become a director upon 
completion of the transactions contemplated by the Plan, or any information that
any such person is adverse to the Company or has a material interest adverse to 
the Company.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 1.25in;text-indent:-
27.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-

#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Less than 1%.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 1.25in;text-indent:-
27.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-
style:italic;">(1)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Unless otherwise
indicated, each stockholder has sole voting and investment power with respect to
all shares of common stock indicated as being beneficially owned by such 
stockholder. Shares of common stock that are not outstanding, but which a 
designated stockholder has the right to acquire within 60&nbsp;days, are 
included in the number of shares beneficially owned by such stockholder and are 
deemed to be outstanding for purposes of determining the percentage of 
outstanding shares beneficially owned by such stockholder, but not for purposes 
of determining the percentage of outstanding shares beneficially owned by any 
other designated stockholder. In all instances where ownership of unvested 
restricted stock is reported below, the individual has the sole power to vote 
such shares but no investment power.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 1.25in;text-indent:-
27.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-

size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>The William 
Herbert Hunt Trust Estate (&#147;WHHTE&#148;) does not directly own any common 
stock; however, as the sole member of Petro-Hunt Holdings,&nbsp;LLC, WHHTE may 
be deemed to indirectly beneficially own the common stock held of record by 
Petro-Hunt Holdings,&nbsp;LLC. The business address for Petro-Hunt 
Holdings,&nbsp;LLC and WHHTE is 2101 Cedar Springs Road, Suite&nbsp;600, Dallas,
Texas&nbsp;75201.</i></p>

style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt 1.25in;text-indent:-
27.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-

#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>According to,

filed by Canada Pension Plan Investment Board (&#147;CPPIB&#148;) and CPP 
Investment Board PMI-2&nbsp;Inc. (&#147;CPPIB PMI-2&#148;) with the SEC on 
June&nbsp;20, 2013 and February&nbsp;10, 2016. CPPIB and CPPIB PMI-2 have shared
voting and dispositive power with respect to 8,775,513 shares of common stock. 
Includes 1,299,600 shares of common stock issuable upon the conversion of 40,000
shares of the Company&#146;s 5.75% Series&nbsp;A Cumulative Perpetual 
Convertible Preferred Stock (the &#147;Series&nbsp;A Preferred Stock&#148;) 
beneficially owned by CPPIB. The business address for each of CPPIB and CPPIB 
PMI-2 is One Queen Street East, Suite&nbsp;2500, Toronto, ON M5C&nbsp;2W5,

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">SECTION&nbsp;16(A)&nbsp;BENEFICIAL 
OWNERSHIP REPORTING COMPLIANCE</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Section&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;of the Exchange Act requires 
our directors, executive officers and persons who beneficially own more than 10%
of our common stock to file certain reports with the SEC concerning their 
beneficial ownership of our equity securities. The SEC&#146;s regulations also 
require that a copy of all such Section&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;forms filed must be 
furnished to us by the executive officers, directors and greater than 10% 
stockholders.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">To our knowledge based solely on a review of copies of
reports filed under Section&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;during the 2015 fiscal year and 
furnished to us, our directors, executive officers and holders of 10% or more of
our shares timely filed reports required by Section&nbsp;16(a), with the 
exception of one Form&nbsp;5 filed late on behalf of Mr.&nbsp;Wilson relating to
a gift of 11,000 shares to the Elijah B. Wilson Trust.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">SECURITYHOLDER COMMUNICATIONS WITH 
THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">Our board welcomes communications from our 
stockholders and other interested parties. Stockholders and any other interested
parties may send communications to our board, to any committee of our board, to 
the Lead Director, or to any director in particular to: c/o Halc&#243;n
Resources Corporation, Attention: Corporate Secretary, 1000 Louisiana St., 
Suite&nbsp;6700, Houston, Texas 77002. Any correspondence addressed to our 
board, to any committee of our board, to the Lead Director, or to any one of the
directors in care of our offices is required to be forwarded to the addressee or
addressees without review by any person to whom such correspondence is not 
addressed.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">CERTAIN RELATIONSHIPS AND RELATED 
TRANSACTIONS</font></b></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Charter of Aircraft</font></i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the ordinary course of its business, the Company 
occasionally charters private aircraft from unaffiliated air charter companies. 
Floyd C. Wilson, the Company&#146;s Chairman and CEO, indirectly owns</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-
align:center;">16<a name="PB_16_035852_141"></a></p>

align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='16',FILE='C:\JMS\109493\16-17636-1\task8084969\17636-1-
be.htm',USER='109493',CD='Aug 30 22:42 2016' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">an aircraft which is managed by an independent air 
charter company unaffiliated with both Mr.&nbsp;Wilson and the Company. The 
Company occasionally charters private aircraft, including the aircraft owned 
indirectly by Mr.&nbsp;Wilson, from this company. The aircraft in the air 
charter company&#146;s fleet, including the aircraft indirectly owned by 
Mr.&nbsp;Wilson, are available to the public for charter based upon a standard 
fee schedule established by the air charter company, with the fees dependent 
primarily upon the type and size of the aircraft utilized and the duration of 
the flight. During 2015, the Company paid a total of approximately $0.5 million 
to the air charter company that manages Mr.&nbsp;Wilson&#146;s aircraft, all of 
which was related to the use of the aircraft indirectly owned by 
Mr.&nbsp;Wilson. Because the air charter company establishes fees for the use of
the aircraft in its fleet, Mr.&nbsp;Wilson does not receive any greater benefit 
from the Company&#146;s charter of the aircraft indirectly owned by him than he 
does if any third party were to charter those aircraft. Any fees related to the 
charter of the aircraft are paid to the air charter company, which deducts from 
revenues received from charter customers a variety of expenses incidental to use
of the aircraft (such as personnel, fuel and commissions) and recurring charges 
(such as for inspections, maintenance, storage and service).</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">The use of charter and Company-owned aircraft by 
Company personnel is governed by the Company&#146;s Aircraft Policy. Our 
policies do not require that a special committee of the Company&#146;s 
independent directors approve the use of aircraft chartered through an 
unaffiliated air charter company that independently establishes the amount
charged under arrangements that otherwise comply with our Aircraft 
Policy.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Related Party Transaction Review 
Policies and Procedures</font></i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">A transaction or series of similar transactions to 
which we are a party in which the amount involved exceeds $120,000 and involves 
a director, executive officer, 5% stockholder or any immediate family members of
these persons is evaluated by a special committee of disinterested directors 
formed by our board of directors to evaluate such transactions. In addition, our
code of conduct provides that every employee should disclose any material 
transaction or relationship that could reasonably be expected to give rise to a 
conflict of interest to upper management or the Company&#146;s Audit Committee. 
The Audit Committee has the authority to evaluate any such conflicts of interest
and recommend actions to be taken by our board in connection with such conflicts
of interest or to report the existence of any such conflicts of interest to the 
full board for it to take action.</font></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p align="center" style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-
align:center;">17<a name="PB_17_040027_723"></a></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade 
align="left" style="color:#010101;"></div>
</div>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(1)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Represents actual base 
salary paid in the year.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(2)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Comprised of annual cash
incentive bonus paid subsequent to year end for prior year performance.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(3)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Represents the grant 
date fair value of awards granted during the indicated year, as determined in 
accordance with ASC Topic 718. Pursuant to SEC rules, the amounts shown exclude 
the impact of estimated forfeitures related to service-based vesting conditions.
Please see the discussion of the assumptions made in the valuation of these 
awards in &#147;Note&nbsp;11&#151;Stockholders&#146; Equity&#148; to the audited
consolidated financial statements included in our annual report on Form&nbsp;10-
K for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015. See &#147;Grants of Plan-Based 
Awards in 2015&#148; for information on awards made in 2015. Generally, the full
grant date fair value is the amount that we would expense in our financial 
statements over the award&#146;s vesting schedule. These amounts reflect our 
accounting expense, and do not correspond to the actual value that will be 
recognized by the named executive officers.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-

#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>For 2015, the amounts 
reported for &#147;All Other Compensation&#148; include amounts provided to the 
named executive officers as outlined in the table below, with respect to 
(a)&nbsp;the matching contribution that we make on account of employee 
contributions under our 401(k)&nbsp;Savings Plan, (b)&nbsp;premiums paid by the 
Company for executive long-term disability insurance, (c)&nbsp;limited tax 
gross-ups for life insurance, parking and country club memberships, and 
(d)&nbsp;country club memberships paid by the Company for Messrs.&nbsp;Wilson 
and Mize.</i></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade 
align="left" style="color:black;"></div>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(1)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Awards granted under the
Plan provide only for a single estimated payout. Under the Plan there are no 
minimum amounts payable for a certain level of performance and there are no 
maximum payouts possible above the target. Thus, there are no thresholds or 
maximums (or equivalent items) applicable to these awards.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(2)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Represents shares of 
restricted stock and stock options issued under the Plan. The shares of 
restricted stock and stock options vest in three equal installments on each 
anniversary of the date of grant, beginning on the first anniversary of the date
of grant, in each case, provided that the recipient has been continuously 
employed at such date.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(3)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>The exercise price of 
each award is equal to the closing market price of our common stock on the date 
of grant.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-
indent:-.5in;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-
size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(4)</font></i><font size="1" style="font-
size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&
#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#1
60;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i>Represents the full 
grant date fair value determined in accordance with ASC Topic 718. Please see 
the discussion of the assumptions made in the valuation of these awards in 
&#147;Note&nbsp;11&#151;Stockholders&#146; Equity&#148; to the audited 
consolidated financial statements included in our annual report on Form&nbsp;10-
K for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015. Generally, the full grant date fair
value is the amount that we would expense in our financial statements over the 
award&#146;s vesting schedule. These amounts reflect our accounting expense, and
do not correspond to the actual value that will be recognized by the named 
executive officers.</i></p>
<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" 
style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
